# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0`, `github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0`, `github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0`, `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd`

82-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Kubernetes API server admission webhook chain and created the answer file. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Components Identified

### **Webhook Plugins (Entry Points)**
- `MutatingAdmissionWebhook` - implements `admission.MutationInterface` 
- `ValidatingAdmissionWebhook` - implements `admission.ValidationInterface`

### **Webhook Call Dispatch**
- **mutatingDispatcher**: Sequentially invokes mutating webhooks, applies JSON patches, handles reinvocation
- **validatingDispatcher**: Invokes validating webhooks in parallel, aggregates results

### **Admission Response Aggregation**
- `CreateAdmissionObjects()` - creates versioned admission review requests
- `VerifyAdmissionResponse()` - validates and extracts webhook responses, aggregating audit annotations and warnings

### **Key Infrastructure Files**
1. Generic webhook base class and interfaces
2. Configuration managers for dynamic webhook loading
3. Webhook accessor patterns for abstraction
4. Reinvocation context for handling webhook reinvocation
5. Match condition evaluation (CEL)
6. Error handling and status conversion

### **Call Flow**
The chain flows from plugin entry points through a generic webhook dispatcher that:
1. Gets webhooks from configuration sources
2. Determines which webhooks should be called (ShouldCallHook)
3. Creates admission review requests
4. Calls webhooks (sequentially for mutating, in parallel for validating)
5. Verifies and aggregates responses
6. Applies mutations or enforces validation decisions

The answer.json file contains complete details with file paths, symbol names, and the full narrative explanation of how the webhook chain architecture works.

Contains the Dispatch() method which retrieves webhooks from the source and invokes the specific dispatcher. Also provides ShouldCallHook() to determine if a webhook should be invoked based on namespace/object selectors and rules matching.\\n\\n**Interfaces** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/generic/interfaces.go): Defines the Dispatcher interface and WebhookInvocation structure that describes how to call a webhook.\\n\\n## Webhook Call Dispatch\\n\\n**mutatingDispatcher** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/dispatcher.go): Implements the Dispatcher interface for mutating webhooks. The Dispatch() method iterates through hooks sequentially, calling callAttrMutatingHook() for each. Handles reinvocation context to support webhook re-invocation when objects are modified. Applies JSON patches to the object and aggregates audit annotations and warnings.\\n\\n**validatingDispatcher** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/validating/dispatcher.go): Implements the Dispatcher interface for validating webhooks. The Dispatch() method collects all relevant hooks, then invokes them in parallel using goroutines. Each hook is called via callHook() independently, with errors collected and returned together.\\n\\n## Request/Response Handling and Aggregation\\n\\n**admissionreview** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/request/admissionreview.go): Handles the creation and verification of admission review objects. CreateAdmissionObjects() creates AdmissionRequest/Response objects in the appropriate version (v1 or v1beta1) based on the webhook's declared versions. VerifyAdmissionResponse() validates the webhook response, checking UID matches, ensuring patch/patchType consistency, extracting audit annotations and warnings, and returning the aggregated AdmissionResponse.\\n\\n## Webhook Configuration Management\\n\\n**Configuration Managers** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/configuration/): Manages dynamic webhook configurations via informers. mutatingWebhookConfigurationManager and validatingWebhookConfigurationManager implement the generic.Source interface, providing lists of webhook accessors from MutatingWebhookConfiguration and ValidatingWebhookConfiguration resources respectively.\\n\\n## Webhook Accessors\\n\\n**WebhookAccessor** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/accessors.go): Abstract interface providing common access patterns to both mutating and validating webhook definitions. Includes methods to get webhook properties, REST clients, namespace/object selectors, match conditions, and rules. Implementations wrap v1.MutatingWebhook and v1.ValidatingWebhook.\\n\\n## Supporting Infrastructure\\n\\n**Reinvocation** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/reinvocationcontext.go): Tracks which webhooks have been invoked and may be reinvoked if mutations occur during the admission chain.\\n\\n**Match Conditions** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/matchconditions/): Compiles and evaluates CEL expressions for webhook match conditions.\\n\\n**Error Handling** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/errors/): Provides error conversion for webhook responses.\\n\\n## Overall Admission Chain Integration\\n\\n**Admission Chain** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/chain.go): The chainAdmissionHandler executes handlers in sequence, supporting both Admit() and Validate() operations.\\n\\n**Reinvocation Handler** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/reinvocation.go): Wraps the admission chain to handle reinvocation of eligible webhooks when mutations occur.\\n\\n## Call Flow\\n\\nFor mutating webhooks: Admit() \u2192 Webhook.Dispatch() \u2192 mutatingDispatcher.Dispatch() \u2192 [for each hook] ShouldCallHook() \u2192 callAttrMutatingHook() \u2192 CreateAdmissionObjects() \u2192 webhook call \u2192 VerifyAdmissionResponse() \u2192 apply patches\\n\\nFor validating webhooks: Validate() \u2192 Webhook.Dispatch() \u2192 validatingDispatcher.Dispatch() \u2192 [parallel for each hook] ShouldCallHook() \u2192 callHook() \u2192 CreateAdmissionObjects() \u2192 webhook call \u2192 VerifyAdmissionResponse() \u2192 aggregate results\\n\"\n}\n",
